# Repository Instructions

## Execution Workflow
- Treat `references/plan.md` as the authoritative implementation plan.
- Always start with the earliest unfinished plan item.
- Break that item into concrete tasks, complete them one at a time, verify each one, and only then move to the next task.
- Update `references/plan.md` only when implementation reality requires a change.

## Remote Sync
- After completing a substantial plan item such as `0.2`, `0.3`, `1.1`, or `3.2`, create a focused commit and push it to `origin` so the remote repository reflects major progress checkpoints.

## Phase Checkpoints
- When an entire phase is complete, create a clearly named GitHub checkpoint for that phase so there is a stable recovery marker for later reference.
- Prefer a GitHub milestone for tracking visibility, and use a git-native checkpoint such as a tag or equivalent marker when an actual rollback point is required.
- Use rollback tags in the format `rollback/phase-<n>-<short-name>` so phase checkpoints are easy to identify and reuse.


## Skills
A skill is a set of local instructions to follow that is stored in a `SKILL.md` file. Below is the list of skills that can be used. Each entry includes a name, description, and file path so you can open the source for full instructions when using a specific skill.
### Available skills
- figma: Use the Figma MCP server to fetch design context, screenshots, variables, and assets from Figma, and to translate Figma nodes into production code. Trigger when a task involves Figma URLs, node IDs, design-to-code implementation, or Figma MCP setup and troubleshooting. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/figma/SKILL.md)
- figma-implement-design: Translate Figma nodes into production-ready code with 1:1 visual fidelity using the Figma MCP workflow (design context, screenshots, assets, and project-convention translation). Trigger when the user provides Figma URLs or node IDs, or asks to implement designs or components that must match Figma specs. Requires a working Figma MCP server connection. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/figma-implement-design/SKILL.md)
- gh-fix-ci: Use when a user asks to debug or fix failing GitHub PR checks that run in GitHub Actions; use `gh` to inspect checks and logs, summarize failure context, draft a fix plan, and implement only after explicit approval. Treat external providers (for example Buildkite) as out of scope and report only the details URL. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/gh-fix-ci/SKILL.md)
- linear: Manage issues, projects & team workflows in Linear. Use when the user wants to read, create or updates tickets in Linear. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/linear/SKILL.md)
- playwright: Use when the task requires automating a real browser from the terminal (navigation, form filling, snapshots, screenshots, data extraction, UI-flow debugging) via `playwright-cli` or the bundled wrapper script. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/playwright/SKILL.md)
- openai-docs: Use when the user asks how to build with OpenAI products or APIs and needs up-to-date official documentation with citations, help choosing the latest model for a use case, or explicit GPT-5.4 upgrade and prompt-upgrade guidance; prioritize OpenAI docs MCP tools, use bundled references only as helper context, and restrict any fallback browsing to official OpenAI domains. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/.system/openai-docs/SKILL.md)
- skill-creator: Guide for creating effective skills. This skill should be used when users want to create a new skill (or update an existing skill) that extends Codex's capabilities with specialized knowledge, workflows, or tool integrations. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/.system/skill-creator/SKILL.md)
- skill-installer: Install Codex skills into $CODEX_HOME/skills from a curated list or a GitHub repo path. Use when a user asks to list installable skills, install a curated skill, or install a skill from another repo (including private repos). (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/.system/skill-installer/SKILL.md)
### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, open its `SKILL.md`. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.

### 74. Assistant

I compared the current branch head `fdef262` against the tip of `codex/engine_development`, which is `ea212b7`. Reading the actual implementation files, not the roadmap, the conclusion is: there are no new power-achievement gains after `ea212b7`. The current branch is functionally at the same power-implementation level; what changed after that checkpoint is mostly code movement, component splitting, hook extraction, and styling cleanup.

**Implemented Powers**
- `Awareness` is implemented as an active `Assess Character` cast plus passive awareness-derived state. The active cast is single-target, CR-gated by `PER + level` with hard caps, and writes an intel snapshot into game history in [combatEncounterCasting.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\combatEncounterCasting.ts). The passive side already includes alertness bonus and temporary inspiration handling in [characterRuntime.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\config\characterRuntime.ts) and [characterTemplate.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\config\characterTemplate.ts). This is the same capability set that already existed on `codex/engine_development`.
- `Body Reinforcement` is implemented as an active effect builder in [powerEffects.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\rules\powerEffects.ts). It supports physical-stat selection and DR bonus when present in the runtime mechanics. Targeting rules are already level-aware. No new behavior was added after `ea212b7`.
- `Healing` is implemented as a healing-resolution pipeline in [powerEffects.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\rules\powerEffects.ts) and applied through [combatEncounterCasting.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\combatEncounterCasting.ts) plus [combatResolution.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\rules\combatResolution.ts). It supports total heal calculation, target limits, allocation across multiple targets, and actual HP restoration. This is unchanged in achievement terms versus `codex/engine_development`.
- `Light Support` is implemented as an aura-style active effect in [powerEffects.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\rules\powerEffects.ts). It grants hit/DR/soak bonuses, supports aura sharing, conflict handling, and target management. This was already in the engine branch and is still the same now.
- `Shadow Control` is partially implemented. `Cloak of Shadow` exists as an active effect with stealth/intimidation/AC bonuses, and `Shadow Manipulation` exists as a direct-damage variant in [powerEffects.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\rules\powerEffects.ts). Aura-sharing support also exists for higher levels. No new crowd-control/paralyze/control mechanics were added after `ea212b7`.
- `Necromancy` is partially implemented. The only executable combat slice is `Necrotic Touch`, with touch-outcome handling, necrotic damage, and self-heal-on-hit flow in [combatEncounterCasting.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\combatEncounterCasting.ts) and [powerEffects.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\rules\powerEffects.ts). That matches the engine branch state.
- The encounter systems that make those powers usable are present in both states: supported-castable-power filtering, variant selection, target-mode logic, aura-source sharing, effect conflict detection, healing allocation, direct-damage application, and replacement warnings. Today that logic lives across [powerEffects.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\rules\powerEffects.ts), [combatEncounterCasting.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\combatEncounterCasting.ts), and the split encounter UI components, but the achievement level is the same as `ea212b7`.

**What Changed After `codex/engine_development`**
- The power rule modules were moved from `src/config/*` to `src/rules/*`. That is structural, not a power-coverage increase.
- The old monolithic encounter power UI was split. The logic that used to sit in `src/components/combat-encounter/CombatantPowerControls.tsx` on `codex/engine_development` is now distributed across [CombatantPowerControls.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\combat-encounter\CombatantPowerControls.tsx), [CombatantCastForm.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\combat-encounter\CombatantCastForm.tsx), [CombatantActiveEffectsPanel.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\combat-encounter\CombatantActiveEffectsPanel.tsx), [useCombatantCastState.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\hooks\useCombatantCastState.ts), and [useAuraEffectManager.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\hooks\useAuraEffectManager.ts). This preserved behavior; it did not add new power implementations.
- The player-character mutation logic and styles were also split, again without adding new power behavior.
- The branch history after `ea212b7` confirms that. The commits are refactor/tech-debt commits, not power implementation commits.

**Still Not Implemented In Either State**
- `Crowd Control` has template text in the sheet model, but there is no executable cast branch for paralyze/control, no status application flow, and no maintenance-turn logic in the current codebase or in `codex/engine_development`.
- `Elementalist` is not implemented as a direct-damage power. It exists in power definitions, but there is no executable branch in the cast-resolution code.
- `Necromancy` summons and `Resurrection` are not implemented.
- The broader healing backlog is not implemented: poison/disease/curse removal, limb regrowth, overheal-to-temp-HP, and the rest of the advanced slice are not present in executable logic.
- The utility backlog is not implemented: `Light Support` nightvision / mana restore / expose darkness, `Body Reinforcement` cantrip stand-up behavior, `Shadow Control` cosmetic cantrips, and similar extras are not present as runtime behavior.
- The `AA` item-identification flow is not implemented as gameplay logic. The data model already contains identification-related fields in [characterTemplate.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\config\characterTemplate.ts), but there is no completed cast/runtime flow around them. That was already true on `codex/engine_development`.

So in plain terms: current `codex/powers-implementation` is a cleaner, more modular version of the `ea212b7` engine state, but it has not advanced the project’s implemented powers beyond what `codex/engine_development` had already achieved.

### 87. Assistant

**Verdict**
I compared branch tips directly in git: `fdef262` on `codex/powers-implementation` versus `ea212b7` on `codex/engine_development`.

In terms of actual power implementation achievements, `codex/powers-implementation` is not ahead of `codex/engine_development`. It keeps the same implemented power slice and mostly refactors the code into cleaner modules.

**Evidence**
- The core implementation surface in [src/config/powerEffects.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\config\powerEffects.ts) on `codex/engine_development` is functionally the same as `src/rules/powerEffects.ts` on `codex/powers-implementation`. The diff there is effectively import-path rewiring, not new mechanics.
- The cast orchestration in [src/lib/combatEncounterCasting.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\combatEncounterCasting.ts) is also functionally unchanged between the branches.
- `powerData.ts` is byte-for-byte identical between the two branches, and `json_refs/powers.json` did not change.
- The power-facing tests in [tests/powerEffects.test.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\tests\powerEffects.test.ts), [tests/combatResolution.test.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\tests\combatResolution.test.ts), and [tests/viewModelSelectors.test.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\tests\viewModelSelectors.test.ts) only changed import paths on `codex/powers-implementation`; they did not gain new power assertions.

**Power-By-Power Comparison**
- `Awareness`: same on both branches. `Assess Character` exists, CR gating exists, and it writes an intel snapshot to game history. No new `AS / AI / AC / AA` split exists on `codex/powers-implementation`.
- `Body Reinforcement`: same on both branches. Physical stat selection works, and higher-level DR bonus logic is already there in both.
- `Healing`: same on both branches. Heal-pool calculation, single/multi-target allocation, and runtime healing application are unchanged. Negative HP healing behavior is also the same.
- `Light Support`: same on both branches. Aura bonuses and aura-sharing behavior are already implemented on `engine_development` and preserved on `powers-implementation`.
- `Shadow Control`: same on both branches. Cloak/self-aura behavior and `Shadow Manipulation` direct damage are already present on `engine_development` and unchanged on `powers-implementation`.
- `Necromancy`: same on both branches. `Necrotic Touch` is present in both, including the touch-attack gate and self-heal on hit. No summon or resurrection implementation was added on `powers-implementation`.
- `Crowd Control`: not implemented on either branch beyond data/template presence.
- `Elementalist`: not implemented on either branch beyond data/template presence.
- `Summons / Resurrection`: not implemented on either branch.
- `Advanced healing slices` like poison/disease/curse removal, limb regrowth, overheal to temp HP: not implemented on either branch.
- `Light Support` cantrip/nightvision, mana restore, `Expose Darkness`: not implemented on either branch.
- `Necromancy` cantrip undead aggro/melee bonus behavior: not implemented on either branch.

**What Actually Changed On `codex/powers-implementation`**
- Rule modules were moved from `src/config/*` to `src/rules/*`.
- `CombatantPowerControls` was split into smaller pieces like `CombatantCastForm`, `CombatantActiveEffectsPanel`, `useCombatantCastState`, and `useAuraEffectManager`.
- `PlayerCharacterPage` mutation logic was extracted into `usePlayerCharacterMutations`.
- Styles were split out of the monolithic CSS.

Those are maintainability refactors, not new power achievements.

So the practical conclusion is: for implemented powers, `codex/powers-implementation` and `codex/engine_development` are functionally at the same level. The newer branch is easier to work in, but it does not advance the power feature set yet.

   - what is present on `codex/powers-implementation`

5. Then continue from the earliest unfinished item in `references/plan.md`

Read first:
- `references/plan.md`

What `codex/engine_development` had already accomplished and should be considered expected baseline:
- player flow
- DM flow
- character sheet
- local persistence
- DM NPC creation
- combat dashboard

- decomposed encounter/player-character components

Your task is not to assume that those are present.
Your task is to verify them and identify gaps.

Map current branch state against `references/plan.md` using this expectation model:

- HP must be allowed to go negative. Do not clamp HP to `0`.

<proposed_plan>
# Power Mechanics Audit and Completion Plan

## Summary
- Audit first, then correct the docs and tracking before touching mechanics.
- The codebase already has the encounter engine, `AS` / `AI` / `AC`, temporary inspiration, temporary HP, typed intel snapshots, status tags, Healing first slice, aura sharing, `Shadow Manipulation`, `Necrotic Touch`, and `Light Support` passive mana bonus.
- Active execution scope is now: finish the remaining T1 power system on `codex/powers-implementation`, but move `AA` out of the active sequence and mark it blocked until a separate item-authoring design exists.

## Roadmap and Tracking Corrections
- Update [plan.md](C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/references/plan.md) to reflect actual repo state:
  - `3.1` is mostly complete already.
  - `3.2` has `AS`, `AI`, and `AC` complete; `AA` moves to a blocked/deferred section tied to future item-authoring work.
  - `3.3` should no longer claim `Necrotic Touch` higher-level mana still needs correction.
  - `3.4` should no longer treat `Light Support` mana cantrip bonus as missing; only the remaining utility behaviors stay open.
- Sync contradictory branch docs after `plan.md`, especially [project_objective.md](C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/references/project_objective.md) and [current_notes.md](C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/references/current_notes.md), because they still describe a pre-encounter branch state.
- Create `/project_tracking/tasks_todo.md`, `/project_tracking/tasks_done.md`, and `/project_tracking/task_log.md`.
- Seed `tasks_todo.md` from the corrected roadmap before implementation starts.
- Move each completed task into `tasks_done.md` immediately after verification.
- Keep `task_log.md` append-only with timestamp, task id/title, files touched, validation run, and any newly discovered follow-up tasks.

## Important Interface and State Changes
- Extend `CharacterDraft` with a structured `powerUsageState`:
  - daily counters
  - long-rest counters
  - per-target daily counters
- Hydrate, normalize, and persist `powerUsageState` through the existing local-storage path.
- Extend `CombatEncounterState` with minimal turn runtime:
  - current round
  - active combatant / turn cursor
  - encounter-only transient combatants for summons
  - encounter-only ongoing states for maintained mechanics that cannot live cleanly on the sheet alone
- Keep transient summons inside encounter state, not in persisted `characters`.
- Extend `PreparedCastRequest` with explicit operation arrays for:
  - resource changes
  - status-tag changes
  - usage-counter updates
  - summon spawn/dismiss actions
- Extend active-effect / combat-resolution support so temporary resistance deltas can exist; this is required for `Expose Darkness`.

## Implementation Sequence
- Shared foundation first:
  - add `powerUsageState`
  - add manual reset actions for daily and long-rest power uses on player and DM-facing sheet surfaces
  - add encounter turn state and transient summon support
  - wire encounter views to resolve combatants from persisted characters plus transient summon records
- Finish direct damage and healing:
  - implement `Elementalist` main cast and cantrip
  - support locked element at Lv1-2, free switching at Lv3+, split-damage rules, extra mana scaling on split casts, Lv5 necrotic unlock, and living-target necrotic vulnerability
  - finish Healing Lv3-5: poison/disease/curse removal, limb-regrowth flag, overheal to temp HP capped by target `STAM`, cantrip wound-mend per-target daily limits
  - keep negative HP behavior unchanged
- Finish passive and utility backlog:
  - add `Crowd Control` cantrip bonuses to derived skill values
  - add `Necromancy` cantrip melee bonus to derived values
  - surface derived non-damage utility traits in sheet/encounter UI: nightvision, hostile-undead aggro priority, techno-invisibility immunity, shadow-walk availability, cosmetic-cantrip availability
  - implement `Light Support` mana restore and `Expose Darkness`
  - implement `Body Reinforcement` delayed stand-up cantrip using the encounter turn state
- Finish control and summons:
  - implement `Crowd Control` contest flow, success-only mana spend, level-based target eligibility, per-turn maintenance, damage-break rules, and controller-linked status tags
  - keep controlled targets in their current party; show `Paralyzed` and `Controlled by <caster>` tags instead of moving parties
  - do not add a full command UI; only add minimal control state plus optional short command note if needed
  - implement `Necromancy` summons, `Shadow Soldier`, and `Resurrection` using transient encounter combatants built from `json_refs/powers.json`
  - `Resurrection` only targets an already loaded character record and restores them to `1 HP`

## Test Plan
- Unit tests for `powerUsageState` hydration, reset behavior, and per-target use limits.
- Unit tests for passive derived bonuses: `Light Support`, `Crowd Control`, `Necromancy`, and Awareness regressions.
- Combat-resolution tests for `Elementalist` split damage, necrotic vulnerability, Healing overheal-to-temp-HP, status removal, delayed revive, `Expose Darkness` resistance downgrades, and `Resurrection`.
- Encounter tests for turn advancement, maintenance mana, control break-on-damage, summon spawn/dismiss, summon initiative behavior, and encounter-only summon lifetime.
- UI/state smoke coverage for cast-form variants, passive trait visibility, reset controls, summon combatants, and control tags.
- Run `npm run typecheck`, `npm test`, and `npm run build` after each substantial task group; record results in `task_log.md`.

## Assumptions and Defaults
- Scope is T1 only, sourced from `references/originals/T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt` and `json_refs/powers.json`.
- `AA` is intentionally deferred and recorded as blocked until a separate item-authoring design exists.
- Daily and long-rest limited abilities use explicit counters with manual reset actions; no automatic calendar or rest engine is added.
- `Resurrection` uses encounter/sheet scope only; the “within 1 hour” rule is manual DM judgment, not auto-enforced.
- Encounter state stays local-only and non-persisted; transient summons and ongoing encounter-only states clear with the encounter.
- When a source rule depends on map/AI systems the app does not have, implement the enforceable mechanical parts and surface the rest as explicit utility state or derived traits instead of silently omitting them.
</proposed_plan>

- Sync contradictory branch docs after `plan.md`, especially [project_objective.md](C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/references/project_objective.md) and [current_notes.md](C:/Users/Evrim/Desktop/FRP/Convergence/game_hub5/references/current_notes.md), because they still describe a pre-encounter branch state.

- Seed `tasks_todo.md` from the corrected roadmap before implementation starts.
- Move each completed task into `tasks_done.md` immediately after verification.
- Keep `task_log.md` append-only with timestamp, task id/title, files touched, validation run, and any newly discovered follow-up tasks.

## Important Interface and State Changes
- Extend `CharacterDraft` with a structured `powerUsageState`:
  - daily counters
  - long-rest counters
  - per-target daily counters
- Hydrate, normalize, and persist `powerUsageState` through the existing local-storage path.
- Extend `CombatEncounterState` with minimal turn runtime:
  - current round
  - active combatant / turn cursor
  - encounter-only transient combatants for summons
  - encounter-only ongoing states for maintained mechanics that cannot live cleanly on the sheet alone
- Keep transient summons inside encounter state, not in persisted `characters`.
- Extend `PreparedCastRequest` with explicit operation arrays for:
  - resource changes
  - status-tag changes
  - usage-counter updates
  - summon spawn/dismiss actions
- Extend active-effect / combat-resolution support so temporary resistance deltas can exist; this is required for `Expose Darkness`.

## Implementation Sequence
- Shared foundation first:
  - add `powerUsageState`
  - add manual reset actions for daily and long-rest power uses on player and DM-facing sheet surfaces
  - add encounter turn state and transient summon support
  - wire encounter views to resolve combatants from persisted characters plus transient summon records
- Finish direct damage and healing:
  - implement `Elementalist` main cast and cantrip
  - support locked element at Lv1-2, free switching at Lv3+, split-damage rules, extra mana scaling on split casts, Lv5 necrotic unlock, and living-target necrotic vulnerability
  - finish Healing Lv3-5: poison/disease/curse removal, limb-regrowth flag, overheal to temp HP capped by target `STAM`, cantrip wound-mend per-target daily limits
  - keep negative HP behavior unchanged
- Finish passive and utility backlog:
  - add `Crowd Control` cantrip bonuses to derived skill values
  - add `Necromancy` cantrip melee bonus to derived values
  - surface derived non-damage utility traits in sheet/encounter UI: nightvision, hostile-undead aggro priority, techno-invisibility immunity, shadow-walk availability, cosmetic-cantrip availability
  - implement `Light Support` mana restore and `Expose Darkness`
  - implement `Body Reinforcement` delayed stand-up cantrip using the encounter turn state
- Finish control and summons:
  - implement `Crowd Control` contest flow, success-only mana spend, level-based target eligibility, per-turn maintenance, damage-break rules, and controller-linked status tags
  - keep controlled targets in their current party; show `Paralyzed` and `Controlled by <caster>` tags instead of moving parties
  - do not add a full command UI; only add minimal control state plus optional short command note if needed
  - implement `Necromancy` summons, `Shadow Soldier`, and `Resurrection` using transient encounter combatants built from `json_refs/powers.json`
  - `Resurrection` only targets an already loaded character record and restores them to `1 HP`

## Test Plan
- Unit tests for `powerUsageState` hydration, reset behavior, and per-target use limits.
- Unit tests for passive derived bonuses: `Light Support`, `Crowd Control`, `Necromancy`, and Awareness regressions.
- Combat-resolution tests for `Elementalist` split damage, necrotic vulnerability, Healing overheal-to-temp-HP, status removal, delayed revive, `Expose Darkness` resistance downgrades, and `Resurrection`.
- Encounter tests for turn advancement, maintenance mana, control break-on-damage, summon spawn/dismiss, summon initiative behavior, and encounter-only summon lifetime.
- UI/state smoke coverage for cast-form variants, passive trait visibility, reset controls, summon combatants, and control tags.
- Run `npm run typecheck`, `npm test`, and `npm run build` after each substantial task group; record results in `task_log.md`.

## Assumptions and Defaults
- Scope is T1 only, sourced from `references/originals/T1_Supernatural_Powers5.txt` and `json_refs/powers.json`.
- `AA` is intentionally deferred and recorded as blocked until a separate item-authoring design exists.
- Daily and long-rest limited abilities use explicit counters with manual reset actions; no automatic calendar or rest engine is added.
- `Resurrection` uses encounter/sheet scope only; the “within 1 hour” rule is manual DM judgment, not auto-enforced.
- Encounter state stays local-only and non-persisted; transient summons and ongoing encounter-only states clear with the encounter.
- When a source rule depends on map/AI systems the app does not have, implement the enforceable mechanical parts and surface the rest as explicit utility state or derived traits instead of silently omitting them.

### 222. Assistant

That is the generic power-usage tracking panel I added.

What it does:
- It reads `sheet.powerUsageState` and builds a small summary in [powerUsage.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\powerUsage.ts).
- It renders that summary in [CharacterResources.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterResources.tsx).

Why it says `No reset-tracked power counters on this sheet yet`:
- This sheet currently has no counters that the summary knows how to show.
- Right now I only wired visible counters for:
  - `Body Reinforcement` revive
  - `Light Support` mana restore
  - `Healing` cantrip target tracking
  - `Healing` overheal tracking

So if the character mainly has powers like `Shadow Control`, `Awareness`, or `Elementalist`, that panel will look empty.

What the buttons do:
- `Reset Daily Uses` clears daily and per-target-daily counters.
- `Reset Long Rest Uses` clears long-rest counters and long-rest selections.
- That reset logic is in [usePlayerCharacterMutations.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\hooks\usePlayerCharacterMutations.ts).

So this is not a mechanic by itself; it is an admin/runtime reset panel. If you want, I can change it so:
- the buttons hide when there is nothing to reset, or
- more powers show visible tracking entries.

- It reads `sheet.powerUsageState` and builds a small summary in [powerUsage.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\powerUsage.ts).
- It renders that summary in [CharacterResources.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterResources.tsx).

Why it says `No reset-tracked power counters on this sheet yet`:
- This sheet currently has no counters that the summary knows how to show.
- Right now I only wired visible counters for:
  - `Body Reinforcement` revive
  - `Light Support` mana restore
  - `Healing` cantrip target tracking
  - `Healing` overheal tracking

So if the character mainly has powers like `Shadow Control`, `Awareness`, or `Elementalist`, that panel will look empty.

What the buttons do:
- `Reset Daily Uses` clears daily and per-target-daily counters.
- `Reset Long Rest Uses` clears long-rest counters and long-rest selections.
- That reset logic is in [usePlayerCharacterMutations.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\hooks\usePlayerCharacterMutations.ts).

So this is not a mechanic by itself; it is an admin/runtime reset panel. If you want, I can change it so:
- the buttons hide when there is nothing to reset, or
- more powers show visible tracking entries.

```
PRE-IMPLEMENTATION WORK

OPERATING RULES
- Read the repository first before changing anything.
- Do not assume the current implementation is correct.
- Do not assume `plan.md` is current.
- Treat existing code, plan files, tracking files, and rule files as inputs to be audited.
- Preserve working behavior unless a change is required by the updated plan or an identified defect.
- Prefer minimal, coherent changes over broad rewrites.
- Keep architecture consistent across combat, powers, items, and character sheets.

REPOSITORY AUDIT REQUIREMENTS
Before implementing:
1. Inspect repository structure.
2. Read `plan.md`.
3. Read all files related to:
   - combat encounter mechanics
   - character sheet state and rendering
   - powers / abilities
   - turn engine / upkeep / status effects
   - item systems / equipment / bonuses
   - shared engine/config/types files
4. Build a dependency map of how these systems interact.
5. Identify:
   - outdated assumptions
   - missing mechanics
   - duplicated logic
   - inconsistent state ownership
   - UI behavior that conflicts with engine logic

SPECIFICATION CHECK
Before implementation begins:
1. Identify any missing specifications.
2. Ask clarification questions once, in a single grouped message.
3. After answers are received, proceed without stopping.
4. If some ambiguity remains, make the smallest reasonable assumption and record it in the task log.

TRACKING RULES
- Use the tracking system at all times.
- If tracking files already exist, extend them instead of replacing them.
- If they do not exist, create:

  /project_tracking
      tasks_todo.md
      tasks_done.md
      task_log.md

- Every discovered task must be written to `tasks_todo.md` before implementation.
- Every completed task must be moved to `tasks_done.md`.
- `task_log.md` must record:
  - assumptions made
  - important implementation decisions
  - blockers
  - partial fixes
  - follow-up work discovered during implementation

PLANNING RULES
Before coding:
1. Audit `plan.md`.
2. Correct outdated or incomplete sections.
3. Expand the plan so it fully covers:
   - power mechanics
   - combat encounter integration
   - character sheet integration
   - item rules and identification flow
   - turn/upkeep interactions
   - state vs derived-state boundaries
4. Break the plan into concrete implementation tasks.
5. Write those tasks into the tracking system before execution begins.

IMPLEMENTATION RULES
For each task:
1. Implement the change.
2. Update all affected files.
3. Verify consistency across engine, state, UI, and tracking files.
4. Mark the task completed immediately after finishing it.

While working:
- continuously check for architectural inconsistencies
- detect broken assumptions between combat, character sheet, items, and powers
- detect missing state transitions
- refactor when needed, but do not refactor unrelated areas
- add newly discovered work into `tasks_todo.md` before continuing

VALIDATION RULES
After each meaningful implementation step:
- verify logic consistency
- verify no affected system was left partially updated
- verify tracking files match actual progress
- verify `plan.md` still matches the implemented direction

If available, run relevant checks/tests/builds.
If a check cannot be run, explicitly record that in `task_log.md`.

COMPLETION CRITERIA
The project is considered complete only when:
- all tasks in `tasks_todo.md` are resolved
- all completed items appear in `tasks_done.md`
- `task_log.md` reflects major assumptions and decisions
- `plan.md` accurately reflects the implemented system
- combat encounter, character sheet, powers, items, and turn/upkeep mechanics are aligned
- no known unresolved blocker remains undocumented

FINAL REPORT
When finished, report:
- updated `plan.md`
- summary of implemented mechanics
- completed task list
- remaining technical debt (if any)
- assumptions made during implementation
- any blocked or deferred work

```
Task: Fix and extend the combat encounter system according to the following Phase 1 requirements.

Important:
- Treat this as a gameplay/mechanics fix task, not a UI polish task only.
- First inspect current combat encounter implementation, current power logic, summon logic, aura logic, and turn/upkeep handling.
- Then implement the fixes below.
- Preserve existing working behavior unless explicitly changed below.
- If a mechanic is currently missing, implement the smallest clean solution that fits the current architecture.

==================================================
PHASE 1 — FIX COMBAT ENCOUNTER
==================================================

1. Shadow Control level 5
Problems:
- I can observe Chain of Shadows, Shadow Manipulation, and Shadow Soldier.
- Shadow Walk says 125m, but there is no casting option.

Required fix:
- Add a working cast option for Shadow Walk at level 5 if it is supposed to be available.
- Verify that its cast requirements, range, and combat-encounter behavior are implemented consistently with the power definition.

2. Healer level 5
Problems:
- It does not cast cantrip more than 2 times.
- Cure and Heal are incorrectly merged.
- At level 3, Heal is using Cure’s mana cost (3 mana).

Required fix:
- Separate Cure and Heal into distinct actions/mechanics.
- Make sure each uses its own mana cost and its own effect.
- Fix cantrip usage logic so the intended number of uses works correctly.

3. Necromancy level 5
Current good behavior:
- All 4 summon options exist.
- Summon creation works.
- Character sheet is created.
- Summons are added to lists.
- Recasting removes previous summons.

Problems / required decisions:
- Skeletons, including king, are receiving group buffs. Verify whether this is intended and keep/fix accordingly.
- Decide and implement whether healing effects damage undead instead of healing them.
  - If yes, redesign healing-vs-undead interaction cleanly.
- Add a Remove Summon option.
- The same Remove Summon option is also needed for Shadow Soldier.

4. Light Support level 5
Current good behavior:
- Other parts work well.

Problem:
- Expose Darkness works incorrectly.
- Target selection is broken.
- It should be possible to apply it to all enemy targets at once.
- When giving allies a bonus, it should apply a debuff to enemies.

Required fix:
- Fix target selection.
- Support multi-enemy targeting where appropriate.
- Correct ally-buff / enemy-debuff behavior.

5. Crowd Control level 5
Current good behavior:
- Up to 3 targets works.

Problems:
- There is no Cancel / release target option.
- Summons such as Shadow Soldier and Zombie appear targetable by CC, but summons should not be valid CC targets.
- CC upkeep mana logic is problematic.
- CC should spend mana on upkeep, not incorrectly at cast time beyond intended rules.
- Advance Turn button currently does not seem to process this correctly.
- Turn engine may be incomplete; inspect current implementation and fix in a future-proof way.

Required fix:
- Add a Cancel / release target option.
- Prevent invalid CC targeting on summons.
- Implement correct upkeep mana behavior:
  - On successful cast, controlled targets enter maintained state.
  - Upkeep cost should be applied by the turn/upkeep system according to the intended rule.
  - If 3 targets are controlled, upkeep cost should scale correctly.
- Inspect Advance Turn behavior and integrate with upkeep handling.

6. Elementalist level 5
Current good behavior:
- Bolt, cantrip, split/fork behavior, extra mana, and damage type handling look good.

Problem:
- It did not hit Shadow Soldier, but it hit Zombie.

Required fix:
- Inspect target filtering and valid-target logic.
- Fix inconsistent behavior against summons / undead / shadow entities according to intended rules.

7. Aura effects
Problem:
- Aura effects from Shadow Control and Light should be removed from all affected allies if the original source disappears.
  Examples:
  - caster dies
  - self-cancel occurs
- Aura effects should apply to all allies by default on initial cast.
- After initial cast, targets should be addable/removable individually.

Required fix:
- Implement source-linked aura cleanup.
- Default initial application = all allies.
- Support later target add/remove behavior.

8. Physical attacks: attack / hit / damage resolution
Required:
- Implement clickable physical attack mechanics in combat encounter.

Use these temporary item/mechanics assumptions for now:
- Brawl attack:
  - makes 2 attacks
  - base damage = STR
- 1 one-handed weapon:
  - makes 1 attack
  - base damage = STR + 2
- 2 one-handed weapons:
  - makes 2 attacks
  - attack DC = 7 instead of general DC 6
  - base damage = STR + 2
- Two-handed weapon:
  - makes 1 attack
  - base damage = STR + 6
- Ranged attack with bow:
  - makes 1 attack
  - base damage = 5

Notes:

- These assumptions are enough for now to implement physical combat resolution.
- Build the solution so it can later be replaced by full item mechanics.

  - Necrotic Touch

- success/failure handling
- effect application
- upkeep/maintenance linkage where relevant
- integration with combat log and encounter state

IMPLEMENTATION APPROACH

```
## Phase 2: Item creation and rules — basics

Task: Design and implement the first version of the item system for the TTRPG app.

Goal:
Create an OOP-based item model that clearly separates:
1. base item properties
2. bonus properties
3. bonus visibility / identification state per character

Scope:
This phase is only for the domain model, rules, and storage shape.
Do NOT build the full UI yet unless a minimal UI stub is needed to support the model.

==================================================
CORE DESIGN
==================================================

1. Item class hierarchy
Create a base `Item` class.

Create item subclasses:
- `Weapon`
- `Armor`
- `Jewel`
- `Mystic`

Create subtype classes where needed.

Examples:
- `Weapon` -> `OneHandedWeapon`, `TwoHandedWeapon`, `BrawlWeapon`, `OversizedWeapon`
- `Armor` -> `LightArmor`, `HeavyArmor`

Subtype classes must define the item’s base visible stats.

Examples:
- `OneHandedWeapon`: base damage = STR + 2
- `TwoHandedWeapon`: base damage = STR + 6
- `BrawlWeapon`: use brawl-style base rules
- `LightArmor`: +2 AC, +1 DR
- `HeavyArmor`: +3 DR

2. Base properties vs bonus properties
Every item must have two separate layers:
- base properties
- bonus properties

Rules:
- Base properties are always visible to everyone.
- Bonus properties are hidden unless identified / known.
- Bonus effects still apply mechanically even if hidden.

3. Bonus properties model
Do NOT model bonuses as child item classes.

Instead:
- every item must contain a `BonusProfile`
- `BonusProfile` contains all possible bonus fields
- the bonus list must be expandable over time
- every bonus field defaults to empty / none / zero

Rules:
- non-magical item = all bonus fields empty
- magical item = one or more bonus fields have values

Example:
- a sword may have base damage from its weapon type
- and bonus values such as `+1 hit`, `+1 damage`

4. Mechanics vs visibility
Mechanical effect and visibility are separate.

Required rule:
- if an item has a bonus, that bonus must apply in gameplay whenever the item is equipped or used
- this is true even if the character cannot currently see the bonus text

==================================================
IDENTIFICATION / KNOWLEDGE MODEL
==================================================

5. Identification per character
Bonus knowledge must be tracked per character, not globally.

Each item must store enough information to know:
- which characters currently see its bonus details
- which characters had learned its bonus details before

Use item id + character ids to support this.

6. AA interaction
If a character does not know an item’s bonus details, the item UI should show an `Identify` button.

Rules:
- `Identify` is clickable only if:
  - the character has AA
  - the character’s AA level is high enough for the item’s level
- otherwise the button is visible but disabled / greyed out

On successful identification:
- that character becomes a knower of the item’s bonus details
- the button changes to `Mask`
- bonus info becomes visible in that character’s item description

7. Mask behavior
If `Mask` is clicked:
- bonus info is removed from the visible item description for that character
- the button changes back to `Identify`

Rules:
- only characters who had learned the item before may hide/show it freely without re-identifying
- characters who never learned it must identify it first or receive shared knowledge

8. Sharing bonus knowledge
A character who knows an item’s bonus details should be able to share that knowledge with another selected character.

Model this now for a future UI flow such as:
- click item
- choose reveal/share
- select target character

After sharing:
- the selected character should also know and see the item’s bonus details

==================================================
IMPLEMENTATION REQUIREMENTS
==================================================

- Use TypeScript
- Keep the model extensible
- Prefer clear domain types, interfaces, and classes
- Use inheritance for item categories
- Use composition for bonuses
- Do not overbuild UI in this phase
- Focus first on:
  - classes
  - interfaces
  - relationships
  - item state
  - identification state
- If useful, also propose a Supabase storage shape

==================================================
DELIVERABLES
==================================================

1. First propose the class/interface design
2. Then implement the item model code
3. Include a short explanation of:
   - why inheritance is used for item categories
   - why composition is used for bonuses
4. If needed, suggest file locations for the new code
5. Keep the implementation aligned with the existing combat/character engine
```

"""Rules: 
- Items must exist as standalone records.
- Character sheets must store references to items, not embedded full item objects.
- Ownership (possession/inventory), and active usage/equipped state must be separate. 
- Item bonuses must apply based on the character currently using/equipping the item, not based on owner.
- Identification / bonus knowledge must be tracked per character, not globally."""

### 315. Assistant

That is the new encounter activity log panel.

What it shows:
- a short action summary
- the timestamp of when that encounter event was recorded

In your example:
- `Cloak of Shadow: t3 affected t3.` means the cast log recorded a cloak application event
- `11:28:17 AM` is the local timestamp for that log entry

Why it looks odd:
- the summary is using fallback target names/ids, so `t3` is the character identifier, not a friendly display label
- for a self-cast cloak, `affected t3` is redundant wording

So this is not a separate mechanic. It is just runtime logging for encounter actions. If you want, I can tighten the phrasing so self-casts read more like:
- `t3 cast Cloak of Shadow on self`
or use display names instead of ids.

# Repository Instructions

## Execution Workflow
- Treat `references/plan.md` as the authoritative implementation plan.
- Always start with the earliest unfinished plan item.
- Break that item into concrete tasks, complete them one at a time, verify each one, and only then move to the next task.
- Update `references/plan.md` only when implementation reality requires a change.

## Remote Sync
- After completing a substantial plan item such as `0.2`, `0.3`, `1.1`, or `3.2`, create a focused commit and push it to `origin` so the remote repository reflects major progress checkpoints.

## Phase Checkpoints
- When an entire phase is complete, create a clearly named GitHub checkpoint for that phase so there is a stable recovery marker for later reference.
- Prefer a GitHub milestone for tracking visibility, and use a git-native checkpoint such as a tag or equivalent marker when an actual rollback point is required.
- Use rollback tags in the format `rollback/phase-<n>-<short-name>` so phase checkpoints are easy to identify and reuse.


## Skills
A skill is a set of local instructions to follow that is stored in a `SKILL.md` file. Below is the list of skills that can be used. Each entry includes a name, description, and file path so you can open the source for full instructions when using a specific skill.
### Available skills
- figma: Use the Figma MCP server to fetch design context, screenshots, variables, and assets from Figma, and to translate Figma nodes into production code. Trigger when the user provides Figma URLs or node IDs, or asks to implement designs or components that must match Figma specs. Requires a working Figma MCP server connection. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/figma-implement-design/SKILL.md)
- gh-fix-ci: Use when a user asks to debug or fix failing GitHub PR checks that run in GitHub Actions; use `gh` to inspect checks and logs, summarize failure context, draft a fix plan, and implement only after explicit approval. Treat external providers (for example Buildkite) as out of scope and report only the details URL. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/gh-fix-ci/SKILL.md)
- linear: Manage issues, projects & team workflows in Linear. Use when the user wants to read, create or updates tickets in Linear. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/linear/SKILL.md)
- playwright: Use when the task requires automating a real browser from the terminal (navigation, form filling, snapshots, screenshots, data extraction, UI-flow debugging) via `playwright-cli` or the bundled wrapper script. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/playwright/SKILL.md)
- openai-docs: Use when the user asks how to build with OpenAI products or APIs and needs up-to-date official documentation with citations, help choosing the latest model for a use case, or explicit GPT-5.4 upgrade and prompt-upgrade guidance; prioritize OpenAI docs MCP tools, use bundled references only as helper context, and restrict any fallback browsing to official OpenAI domains. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/.system/openai-docs/SKILL.md)
- skill-creator: Guide for creating effective skills. This skill should be used when users want to create a new skill (or update an existing skill) that extends Codex's capabilities with specialized knowledge, workflows, or tool integrations. (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/.system/skill-creator/SKILL.md)
- skill-installer: Install Codex skills into $CODEX_HOME/skills from a curated list or a GitHub repo path. Use when a user asks to list installable skills, install a curated skill, or install a skill from another repo (including private repos). (file: C:/Users/Evrim/.codex/skills/.system/skill-installer/SKILL.md)
### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with `$SkillName` or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
  1) After deciding to use a skill, open its `SKILL.md`. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
  2) When `SKILL.md` references relative paths (e.g., `scripts/foo.py`), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
  3) If `SKILL.md` points to extra folders such as `references/`, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
  4) If `scripts/` exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
  5) If `assets/` or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
  - If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
  - Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
  - Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
  - Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from `SKILL.md` unless you're blocked.
  - When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.

- `Shadow Soldier: Alice created Shadow Soldier.`
- `Remove Summon: Alice dismissed an active summon.`
- `Resurrection: Alice restored Bob.`
- `Light Aura: Alice affected Alice.`
- `Cloak of Shadow: Alice affected Alice.`
- `Expose Darkness: Alice affected Guard, Cultist.`
- `Alice hit Guard with One-Handed Weapon (1 hit).`
- `Alice missed Guard with Bow.`
- `Body Reinforcement revived Bob.`
- `Aura effects ended because Alice is down.`

So it is meant to be a very short DM-facing action history, not full detail text.

## My request for Codex:
i just cast a br lvl5 to a chacarter, it did not appear there

### 326. Assistant

That is a bug.

Cause: the generic buff-cast logger is hardcoded incorrectly in [combatEncounterCasting.ts](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\combatEncounterCasting.ts). For non-`Light Support` casts, it falls back to `Cloak of Shadow` instead of using the actual power name, so `Body Reinforcement` is not logged correctly.

So a `BR Lv5` cast currently goes through the generic effect path, but the summary label logic is wrong. It should produce something like:
- `Body Reinforcement: Alice affected Bob.`

Instead, the code currently only knows:
- `Expose Darkness`
- `Light Aura`
- else `Cloak of Shadow`

That needs fixing.

### 341. Assistant

Current behavior stacks both tags for Crowd Control:

- `Controlled by <caster>`

- one combined tag, or
- only `Controlled by X`, or
- only `Paralyzed`

Given what you just said, the desired behavior is:
- show either `Paralyzed` or `Controlled by X`, not both.

## My request for Codex:
how does physical attacks work? what do i do to make a physical attack? if ihave 2 attacks, can i use one of them on a character and the second on another character?

### 349. Assistant

I’m checking the physical-attack form so I can answer how it currently works in the UI and whether split targets are supported.

### 350. Assistant

I’m checking the physical-attack form so I can answer how it currently works in the UI and whether split targets are supported.

### 351. Assistant

Current behavior is:

- Open a combatant in the encounter.
- In `Physical Attacks`, choose:
  - `Attack Style`
  - `Target`
  - `Hits Landed`
- Then click `Resolve Physical Attack`.

What the form does:
- `Attack Pool` and `Success DC` are just shown to help you roll manually.
- The app does not roll physical attacks for you.
- You roll externally / with the dice helper, decide how many hits landed, then enter that number.
- The app then applies damage to the selected target.

Current attack styles:
- `Brawl`: always available, 2 attacks, damage per hit = `STR`
- `One-Handed Weapon`: 1 attack, damage = `STR + 2`
- `Two One-Handed Weapons`: 2 attacks, damage = `STR + 2`, DC `7`
- `Two-Handed Weapon`: 1 attack, damage = `STR + 6`
- `Oversized Weapon`: 1 attack, damage = `STR + 9`
- `Bow`: 1 attack, damage = `5`

Important limitation:
- No, right now if you have `2 attacks`, you cannot split them between two different targets.
- The current UI/engine supports only one target per physical attack action.
- So if you enter `2` landed hits, both hits go to the same selected target.

### 352. Assistant

Current behavior is:

- Open a combatant in the encounter.
- In `Physical Attacks`, choose:
  - `Attack Style`
  - `Target`
  - `Hits Landed`
- Then click `Resolve Physical Attack`.

What the form does:
- `Attack Pool` and `Success DC` are just shown to help you roll manually.
- The app does not roll physical attacks for you.
- You roll externally / with the dice helper, decide how many hits landed, then enter that number.
- The app then applies damage to the selected target.

Current attack styles:
- `Brawl`: always available, 2 attacks, damage per hit = `STR`
- `One-Handed Weapon`: 1 attack, damage = `STR + 2`
- `Two One-Handed Weapons`: 2 attacks, damage = `STR + 2`, DC `7`
- `Two-Handed Weapon`: 1 attack, damage = `STR + 6`
- `Oversized Weapon`: 1 attack, damage = `STR + 9`
- `Bow`: 1 attack, damage = `5`

Important limitation:
- No, right now if you have `2 attacks`, you cannot split them between two different targets.
- The current UI/engine supports only one target per physical attack action.
- So if you enter `2` landed hits, both hits go to the same selected target.

## My request for Codex:
ok this is not what i want. i want this:
- attcker selects attack --> selects target --> system resolves attack.
- the attacker's weapon choice is already know (given in the charactersheet's loadout).
- the attacker's all attack info (hit, dmg) is known (stats, skills, item bonuses, power buffs, etc.)
- the defender's (selected target by the attacker) all defence info (ac, dr, soak etc.) is known.
- since the system knows all these info, it resolves the attack step by step:
attacker's roll > attacker's hit success > defender's ac comparison > marginal calculation > adding marginal to the damage roll > attacker's damage roll > attacker's dmg success > defender's DR comparison > net damage > net damage reflection to defender's HP. Of course, that will be reflected to the encoutner activity: attacker's hit success, attacker's dmg success, net damage (or damage taken).

### 354. Assistant

That is a different system than what is currently implemented.

Current implementation:
- manual-assisted resolution
- you choose attack style
- you choose target
- you manually enter `hits landed`
- system only applies resulting damage

What you want:
- full automatic attack pipeline
- weapon inferred from loadout
- attack and defense stats derived automatically
- hit roll and damage roll both resolved by the system
- encounter log records intermediate results, not just final action text

So this is not a small tweak. It means replacing the current physical attack flow with a real combat-resolution engine.

What would need to change:
- remove manual `Hits Landed`
- infer attack mode from equipped/active weapon state
- add formal hit-resolution and damage-resolution steps
- define exact formulas for:
  - attack roll pool
  - AC comparison
  - marginal success to bonus damage
  - damage roll pool
  - DR / soak mitigation
- expand encounter activity logging to show step results

Also, one spec gap still exists:
- you said the system should compare against `AC, DR, soak etc.`
- I need the exact formula/order for physical attacks in your rules, especially:
  - how hit success is calculated
  - how AC reduces/blocks the hit
  - how marginal converts into damage bonus
  - how damage success is calculated
  - how DR and soak interact

If you want, I can add this as a TODO now, but I would treat it as a new combat-engine task, not a bugfix.

What each one is right now:
- History size: bug. It is hard-capped by CSS right now, so it cannot grow properly. Added `P1-UI-02`.
- `Shadow Soldier` mana: bug. The current summon data resolves it at `0` mana, so no mana is spent. Added `P1-BUG-03`.
- `Shadow Soldier` auto-aura inheritance: not implemented. Aura sharing is only applied when the aura is cast, not when a later summon appears. Added `P1-RULE-02`.
- `Expose Darkness`: yes, current code treats it as a separate cast/action. That does not match the behavior you just described. Added `P1-RULE-03`.
- `Crowd Control` contest: yes, current code is manual and expects contest input from the UI. It is not auto-rolled. Added `P1-RULE-04`.

About `BR` cantrip:
- There is no manual activation UI for it right now.
- The current implementation treats it as a passive auto-revive trigger, not a selectable cast.
- At `BR 5`, it is supposed to auto-stand the character back up with `4 HP` after turn advance if the trigger conditions are met.

If you want, I can also add a separate TODO to surface BR cantrip state/trigger visibly in the encounter UI.

  - max visible size = 18 rows if max height is kept.
  - remove the current too-small cap that blocks resizing after about 3 rows.
- Tests:
  - CSS-only; validate by build and manual smoke.

## Validation and Tracking
- After each change group, run:
  - `npm run typecheck`
  - `npm test`
  - `npm run build`
- Recommended validation groups:
  1. docs/tracking reopen
  2. `P1-BUG-01` + `P1-BUG-03`
  3. `P1-RULE-04` + `P1-BUG-02`
  4. `P1-RULE-01`
  5. `P1-RULE-02` + `P1-RULE-03`
  6. `P1-UI-01` + `P1-UI-02`
- After each successful group:
  - remove completed items from [tasks_todo.md](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\project_tracking\tasks_todo.md)
  - append concise completion notes to [tasks_done.md](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\project_tracking\tasks_done.md)
  - append implementation notes and validation results to [task_log.md](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\project_tracking\task_log.md)

## Assumptions Locked
- Crowd Control auto-contest uses current derived stats, existing d10 pool rules, and fails on ties.
- Encounter-visible Crowd Control tag is `Controlled by <caster>`.
- `Expose Darkness` is no longer a separate encounter cast; it becomes the enemy-side portion of Light Aura Lv5.
- Light Aura Lv5 target management covers both allied buff targets and enemy debuff targets after the initial cast.
- Undead inversion applies to true undead only; `Shadow Soldier` remains `shadow`, not `undead`.
- BR cantrip manual activation/visibility is not part of this pass because it is not in the current actionable Phase 1 TODO list.
- No new UI test framework is introduced in this pass.
</proposed_plan>

# Tasks TODO

## Phase 1: Combat Encounter
- `P1-BUG-01` Fix encounter activity log labels for generic buff casts so they use the actual power/action name. Current defect: `Body Reinforcement` casts do not log correctly and can fall back to `Cloak of Shadow`.
- `P1-UI-01` Replace the inline `Physical Attacks` and `Cast Power Mechanism` sections in the encounter character card with a single `Actions` popover/button. Target layout: `Character Sheet`, `Actions`, `Applied Effects`.
- `P1-BUG-02` Adjust Crowd Control status-tag presentation so a target does not show both `Paralyzed` and `Controlled by <caster>` at the same time. Show only one of them per target.
- `P1-RULE-01` Finalize undead interaction rules in encounter resolution: healing effects should damage undead instead of healing them, and necrotic damage on undead should heal undead targets.
- `P1-UI-02` Fix the encounter history panel sizing. It should open at 3 visible rows minimum, allow vertical expansion beyond that, and cap at 18 rows if a max is kept.
- `P1-BUG-03` Fix `Shadow Soldier` mana consumption. Current level 5 `Shadow Control` summon flow resolves with 0 mana cost.
- `P1-RULE-02` When `Cloak of Shadow` aura is active, newly created `Shadow Soldier` summons should automatically inherit the aura benefits if they are allied recipients of the active aura.
- `P1-RULE-03` Rework `Light Support` level 5 so enemy debuffing is the automatic enemy-side portion of `Light Aura`, not a separate `Expose Darkness` cast.
- `P1-RULE-04` Rework `Crowd Control` encounter casting to auto-resolve the contest in-system using `CHA + INT` for the caster and `CHA + WITS` for each target. Remove manual contest outcome selection.

- `ARCH-REM-01` Later refactor reminder: extract an encounter controller/engine layer from `CombatEncounterPage.tsx` so cast execution, turn advance, upkeep, aura cleanup, summon lifecycle, and encounter log creation move out of the route; keep the route mostly as state wiring and rendering.

## Blocked / Deferred
- `B01` Expand the shared item UI into a full item-authoring and multi-target knowledge-sharing flow.

# Character Sheet Derived Summary Consolidation

    - `Utility Traits`
    - `Combat Flags`
    - `Power Tracking`

  - render the four subsections under the combat grid, in this order:
    1. `Active Effects`
    2. `Utility Traits`
    3. `Combat Flags`
    4. `Power Tracking`
  - keep `Power Tracking` reset buttons in this section
  - show all four subsections even when empty
  - preserve current empty-state copy for `Power Tracking`
  - add matching empty-state copy for:
    - `Active Effects`: no active effects
    - `Utility Traits`: no utility traits
- In [CharacterResources.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterResources.tsx):
  - remove the `Combat Flags` and `Power Tracking` blocks
  - keep only the existing `Resources` content and runtime editing for inspiration / karma
  - drop now-unused props from the component interface
- In [PlayerCharacterPage.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\routes\PlayerCharacterPage.tsx):
  - move the `powerUsageSummary`, `canManagePowerUsage`, and reset callback wiring from `CharacterResources` to `CharacterCombatSummary`
- In [player-character.css](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\styles\pages\player-character.css):
  - create one consistent subsection style inside `Derived Summary`
  - reuse existing visual language from `active-effects-panel` / `resistance-grid` where possible

  - ensure mobile layout still stacks cleanly

  - reset buttons still work from the new location
  - empty character sheets still show empty subsection copy
  - DM runtime editing for resources and combat summary still behaves as before

## Assumptions

- Empty subsection behavior is locked to `show all empty`.
- No new UI test framework should be introduced for this change.

### 521. Assistant

<proposed_plan>
# Character Sheet + Encounter Follow-Up Plan

## Summary
- Add three new tracked tasks before implementation:
  - `CS-UI-01` Move `Active Effects`, `Utility Traits`, `Combat Flags`, and `Power Tracking` into `Derived Summary`.
  - `CS-RULE-01` Replace manual-assisted physical attacks with full automatic physical attack resolution.
  - `CS-UX-01` Replace passive-only `Body Reinforcement` cantrip revival with a visible manual encounter trigger.
- Keep this as a focused follow-up pass. Do not touch `ARCH-REM-01` or `B01`.
- Preserve existing combat and character-sheet behavior unless this plan explicitly changes it.

## Key Changes
### 1. Derived Summary consolidation
- `CharacterCombatSummary` becomes the single home for:
  - combat stat grid
  - `Active Effects`
  - `Utility Traits`
  - `Combat Flags`
  - `Power Tracking`
- `CharacterResources` keeps only stored-state resources such as inspiration and karma.
- Subsection order is fixed:
  1. `Active Effects`
  2. `Utility Traits`
  3. `Combat Flags`
  4. `Power Tracking`
- Empty-state behavior is fixed to `show all empty`.
  - Keep the existing `Power Tracking` empty copy.
  - Add explicit empty copy for `Active Effects` and `Utility Traits`.
- Required interface change:
  - move `powerUsageSummary`, `canManagePowerUsage`, and reset handlers from `CharacterResources` props to `CharacterCombatSummary` props.
- Styling:
  - create a shared subsection pattern inside `Derived Summary`
  - keep the larger card readable on desktop and stacked cleanly on mobile

### 2. Loadout-driven physical attack engine
- Replace the current encounter physical-attack flow:
  - remove manual `Attack Style`
  - remove manual `Hits Landed`
  - keep only `Target` + `Resolve Attack`
- Use the existing loadout model, but normalize weapon handling around explicit canonical slots:
  - `weapon_primary`
  - `weapon_secondary`
- Slot rules:
  - `two_handed`, `oversized`, and `bow` occupy both weapon slots
  - `one_handed` occupies one slot
  - `brawl` maps to the brawl profile
  - if no weapon is equipped, use brawl/fists
  - no separate active-weapon selector
  - item bonuses still stack globally from all applicable equipped/active items
- Attack profile inference is fixed:
  - two occupied `one_handed` weapons => dual one-handed profile
  - exactly one `one_handed` weapon => one-handed profile
  - any `two_handed` / `oversized` / `bow` occupying the weapon slots => that profile
  - otherwise => brawl profile
- Resolution model is fixed:
  - one encounter action selects one target
  - multi-attack profiles still resolve against that same target in v1
  - structure the resolver so future split-target support can be added without changing the UI contract
- Physical-attack math is fixed:
  - hit roll pool = derived attack pool from the inferred profile
  - hit roll DC = profile DC (`6`, or `7` for dual one-handed)
  - if hit successes do not exceed target `AC`, that attack misses
  - marginal = `hit successes - target AC`
  - damage roll pool = inferred base damage pool + marginal
  - damage roll DC = `6`
  - net damage = `damage successes - target DR`, minimum `0`
  - net damage applies through temporary HP first, then HP
- Multi-attack profiles:
  - brawl and dual one-handed resolve as two independent attack sequences against the same selected target
  - each sequence gets its own hit roll, marginal, damage roll, and net damage
- Encounter activity log format:
  - one compact log entry per attack action
  - include enough detail to show each sequence result:
    - hit successes
    - target AC
    - marginal
    - damage successes
    - target DR
    - net damage or miss
- Required interface/type changes:
  - remove `landedHits` from the physical-attack request path
  - replace the current `preparePhysicalAttackRequest` output with an automatic multi-sequence resolver result
  - keep using `PreparedCastRequest` so physical attacks still flow through the existing encounter execution path

### 3. Body Reinforcement cantrip becomes manually triggerable
- Change the current BR revive behavior:
  - stop treating it as an automatic turn-advance revive
  - remove the automatic `body_reinforcement_revive` scheduling/advance behavior from the encounter loop
- New behavior:
  - when a character has `Body Reinforcement >= 2`
  - and current HP is between `0` and `-5`
  - and the daily BR revive use is not spent
  - show a manual encounter action button
- Button behavior:
  - visible in encounter actions for the downed BR character
  - label should be explicit, for example `Trigger Body Reinforcement`
  - on click, immediately restore HP:
    - `1 HP` at BR `2-4`
    - `4 HP` at BR `5`
  - increment the daily BR revive usage counter
  - add a clear encounter log entry
- UI visibility:
  - when not yet eligible, show BR cantrip state in the encounter view as unavailable rather than invisible
  - the implementer should surface:
    - whether the cantrip exists
    - whether it is already spent
    - whether the current HP window makes it triggerable
- Required type/logic change:
  - remove `body_reinforcement_revive` from ongoing-state use if it becomes unused after this change

## Test Plan
- Tracking first:
  - add `CS-UI-01`, `CS-RULE-01`, and `CS-UX-01` to TODO before coding
  - move each to done only after `typecheck`, `test`, and `build` all pass
  - log the slot-model and BR-trigger decisions in `task_log.md`
- Automated coverage:
  - add/update physical-attack tests for:
    - loadout-to-profile inference
    - dual one-handed DC `7`
    - brawl / one-handed / two-handed / oversized / bow profile mapping
    - single-target two-sequence resolution
    - miss case
    - marginal-to-damage case
    - DR reducing damage to zero
    - encounter log content
  - add/update BR tests for:
    - eligibility helper
    - manual trigger consumes daily use
    - HP result at BR `2-4` and BR `5`
    - ineligible states do not trigger
  - add/update character-sheet render or smoke coverage only if there is already a lightweight path; otherwise rely on build plus manual smoke for the Derived Summary move
- Manual smoke:
  - `Derived Summary` shows all four subsections
  - `CharacterResources` no longer shows `Combat Flags` or `Power Tracking`
  - encounter attack form shows target-only flow and resolves automatically
  - BR button/state is visible and understandable in the encounter UI
- Validation after each task group:
  - `npm run typecheck`
  - `npm test`
  - `npm run build`

## Assumptions
- `Bow` occupies both weapon slots.
- No left-hand vs right-hand bonus logic is introduced.
- Global equipped/active item bonuses continue to stack normally.
- Physical attacks use `DR`, not `soak`.
- Multi-attack splitting across multiple targets is intentionally deferred, but the resolver should be structured for it.
- No new UI test framework should be introduced for this pass.
</proposed_plan>

## My request for Codex:
let's start with combat summary. what determines its positioning in derived summary?

### 613. Assistant

`Combat Summary` positioning inside `Derived Summary` is determined by two things:

- The markup order in [CharacterCombatSummary.tsx:38](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterCombatSummary.tsx:38)
  - `Combat Summary` is the first child after the heading, via `<div className="combat-grid">`
  - the subsection block comes after it, via `<div className="derived-summary-subsections">`

- The CSS layout of the card in [player-character.css:284](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\styles\pages\player-character.css:284) and [player-character.css:299](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\styles\pages\player-character.css:299)
  - `.combat-card` makes the whole card span full width
  - `.combat-grid` controls the internal placement of the `Combat Summary` tiles with:
    - `display: grid`
    - `grid-template-columns: repeat(3, minmax(0, 1fr))`
    - `gap`
    - `margin-top`

So:
- vertical position is determined by JSX order
- horizontal tile layout is determined by `.combat-grid`
- the width of the whole parent card is determined by `.combat-card`

# Context from my IDE setup:

## Active file: src/styles/pages/player-character.css

## Active selection of the file:
.combat-card {
  grid-column: 1 / -1;
}
## Open tabs:
- player-character.css: src/styles/pages/player-character.css
- CharacterCombatSummary.tsx: src/components/player-character/CharacterCombatSummary.tsx
- tasks_todo.md: project_tracking/tasks_todo.md

## My request for Codex:
`.combat-card { 
  grid-column: 1 / -1;
}` 
".combat-card makes the whole card span full width " how?

### 616. Assistant

Because `.combat-card` is a child of `.sheet-grid`, and `.sheet-grid` is a CSS grid container.

Relevant rule:
- [player-character.css:257](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\styles\pages\player-character.css:257)
  - `.sheet-grid { grid-template-columns: 1.2fr 1.2fr 0.95fr; }`

That means the page has 3 grid columns.

Then:
- [player-character.css:284](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\styles\pages\player-character.css:284)
  - `.combat-card { grid-column: 1 / -1; }`

`grid-column: 1 / -1` means:
- start at grid line `1`
- end at the last grid line `-1`

In a 3-column grid, that makes the item stretch across all columns, so the whole `Derived Summary` card spans the full available width of the grid.

- [player-character.css:284](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\styles\pages\player-character.css:284)
  - `.combat-card { grid-column: 1 / -1; }`

- start at grid line `1`
- end at the last grid line `-1`

### 619. Assistant

I’m checking the current history rendering and AC snapshot flow so I can answer from the code, not from assumption.

### 620. Assistant

I’m checking the current history rendering and AC snapshot flow so I can answer from the code, not from assumption.

### 621. Assistant

Right now, `t5` does **not** get the full detailed snapshot in the UI.

What currently happens:
- `Assess Character` creates a full `intel_snapshot` entry and stores it in the **caster’s** character sheet `gameHistory`.
- That write happens in [combatEncounterCasting.ts:397](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\lib\combatEncounterCasting.ts:397).
- The snapshot includes detailed fields like:
  - `CR`, `Rank`, `Age`, `Karma`
  - resistances
  - combat summary
  - stats
  - skills
  - powers
  - specials
  - notes

But the current renderer only shows the short summary:
- [CharacterHistorySection.tsx:46](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterHistorySection.tsx:46)
- for `intel_snapshot`, it renders only:
  - `sourcePower`
  - `targetName`
  - `summary`

So in your example, `t5` only sees:
- `Assess Character Lv 5: op1`
- `CR 2, Rank E`

Not the full detail block.

So the answer is:
- the detailed information is being **saved**
- but it is **not being displayed yet** in `Game History`

If you want, I can add a TODO for “render full intel snapshot details in Character Sheet > Game History.”

  - `CR`, `Rank`, `Age`, `Karma`
  - resistances
  - combat summary
  - stats

  - powers
  - specials
  - notes

But the current renderer only shows the short summary:
- [CharacterHistorySection.tsx:46](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\components\player-character\CharacterHistorySection.tsx:46)

So in your example, `t5` only sees:

Not the full detail block.

So the answer is:
- the detailed information is being **saved**

### 632. Assistant

It is a structural refactor reminder, not a gameplay feature.

Right now too much encounter logic still lives directly in:
- [CombatEncounterPage.tsx](C:\Users\Evrim\Desktop\FRP\Convergence\game_hub5\src\routes\CombatEncounterPage.tsx)

That route currently handles things like:

- physical attack execution
- turn advance
